So I will ask you a follow up where does Genesis 3:15 say that because enmity between the woman and the serpent therefore Mary is sinless and lived a sinless life? You are just assuming the very thing you are suppose to be proving.. This is called a fallacy of begging the question.  You assume Genesis 3:15 means sinless Mary and therefore Romans 3:23 does not mean All have sinned with the exception of Jesus in context...instead you add an additional sinless exception that Paul makes NO MENTION of. Ask yourself this...would you assume and get out of the text of Genesis 3:15 that Mary is sinless by just reading the text? Of course not instead the Catholic church (or Catholic  apologists) have suggested you to read it to mean that even though it says absolutely nothing about Mary being sinless. But if you read Romans 3:23 in context absolutely you will come to the conclusion Paul is teaching ALL of humanity have sinned and fallen short of the glory of God with the exception of the one both man and divine...the man Christ Jesus. As for your canon question it makes no sense as of course you believe all Scripture is breathed out by God right? 2nd Tim 3:16...so the divinely inspired Scripture is written down and it matters not that it took a period of time for Christians to RECOGNIZE what God had already given. At the time of writing 2nd Timothy Paul is about to die (he says so in book of Timothy) so we know all of Pauls writings have already been written and almost all of Scripture had been written by then with the possible exceptions of a few books like John or Revelation (depending on when you date those). One God, One Divine Nature:  The Scripture consistently emphasizes that God is one (Deuteronomy 6:4).Â   This oneness of God is understood as a unity of divine essence or nature.Â   2. Three Distinct Persons:  The Bible identifies God as Father, Son (Jesus Christ), and Holy Spirit.Â   These are distinct persons, not just different manifestations of the same person.Â   Examples include the baptism of Jesus (Matthew 3:16-17), where all three persons are present.Â   The Great Commission (Matthew 28:19) also refers to the Father, Son, and Holy Spirit as distinct entities.Â   3. Shared Divine Nature:  While distinct, the Father, Son, and Holy Spirit are described as sharing the same divine attributes and glory.Â   They are all called God (John 1:1, 14; Acts 5:3-4).Â   Genesis 1:26 Then God said, â€œLet US make mankind in our image, in our likeness..  They all participate in works of creation and salvation.Â   For example, Jesus claims to be one with the Father (John 10:30), and the Holy Spirit is called the Spirit of God and the Spirit of Christ.Â   This shared divine nature is what allows the three persons to be considered one God. If you're looking for something even more difficult for challenging yourself with pushups or any workout, I strongly strongly suggest studying isometrics. What you're doing is called isotonics which consists of concentric and eccentric extensions of muscles. However isometrics are different because there is no extension of the muscle. As a example rather then doing 120 pushups, try to do 1 pushup for 3 minutes. Meaning from the start position you set a timer for 3 minutes to start or 2 depending how strong you are. If you can go down and back up but make it take 2 minutes for 1 push up your gains will be insane. This is the most anime protagonist workout possible for humans. Good luck and if you have questions feel free to ask.   Isometrics are the key.
